text:
Definitely 5 star!  Used sirloin steak that sat in the fridge with steak seasoning on it for a day and a half to really absorb the flavors.  BBQ the sirloin rare and then thinly sliced it and set aside in preparation for assembly.  Carmelized the onions prior to making the sandwiches, then sauteed the peppers using green and red for color.  Added mushrooms for a more true Philly sandwich.  Used a variety of cheese; Manchego, Monterey and Mozarella.  My favorite was the Manchego which gave it an edge.  Baked the sandwiches open faced for 5 minutes to crisp the buns, then broiled until the cheese melted, bubbled and slightly browned.  The garlic mayo made the sandwich!  My family loved it.  Thanks Tera for the great recipe.

Superb. Based on comments read and my one Philly Phriend, I made six sandwiches. Two with provolone, two with mozarella, and (Philly) two with cheeze whiz. Provolone and mozarella were equal in outstanding taste. The cheeze whiz was good but not up to the others. Used everything the recipe called for except (above) and low fat mayo. Reheated leftovers in the oven, put in while heating to 500, when reached 500 took out, perfect. Micorwaved leftover sandwiches were not so good.

text:
Well what a nice treat this sandwich was tonight, I savored every single bite of it. I used some top sirloin steak cut very thin, recommend by my butcher. I did marinate the meat for a few hours in some Teriyaki sauce and spices. I also made the mayo/garlic up early so it had time for the flavors to meld together. I didn't want to over cook the meat, so I cooked in this order: The onions first until tender, then added the bell peppers for a few minutes and then the mushrooms, pushing each one aside as I added the next. The last thing I cooked was my sirloin meat until just turning brown, only a few minutes... then stirred it all together and let it cook about another minute. I also lightly buttered my roll prior to plopping my steak and pepper mixture on them. Put slices of Mozzarella on top of the meat mixture and then open faced under the broiler on low for just a few minutes, my oven was already hot since I made some fries. Kept a close eye and as soon as the cheese was melted I removed them. Generously spread the garlic mayonnaise on the top part of the bun. And I must say I'm not a great fan of mayonnaise but it made these sandwiches go over the top. I also think the little butter spread on the buns was a great addition to the flavor. My husband was a very happy man tonight! Thanks Tera.

text:
This is not your traditional "Philly" cheesesteak. And all the changes everyone is making takes it even further away from a real Philly cheesesteak. That's ok. If you can't get the real thing it's ok to try and duplicate. Number one rule is you must have a superior hoagie roll or you've lost half of the battle. Number 2, use top round chipped steak. The rest is up to you, and cheese whiz is a rule in Philly but, I don't care for it. And, if you're ever in Philly, best place to go for anykinda sandwich is Tony Luke's..

text:
My family loved this, but I did make some changes. I used skirt steak instead of round steak. I also used sliced mozzarella instead of shredded. I thought that putting the sandwiches in a 500 degree oven would make the buns too hard so I wrapped each sandwich in foil and put them in a 350 degree oven for approx. 8 minutes till the cheese was melted and they came out perfect! I did have some mayo mix left over and will make a little less of this mixture next time. It may not be the original Philly Cheesesteak, but it's still a great recipe!

Delicious.  I know it is not Philly-style, but it is so good. If you use the round, you should really marinate for awhile in meat tenderizer with some Montreal Steak seasoning. Only if you use a very tender sirloin can you get away with not marinading/tenderizing.  Another trick is to use your sharp knife and just keep mincing till the beef bits are very small.

WOW!!! My husband and I absolutely loved this one, and the garlic mayo totally made the sandwich! We made a couple of very slight changes- seared the steaks on the grill; sauteed the veggies while they grilled, then combined; also, we used garlic salt instead of plain, added right after toss-frying the sliced steak and veggies together, to blend the flavors and heat it back up. The mayo was the PERFECT touch- we made it as stated in the recipe- that may be our new favorite condiment! The garlic keeps its fresh, spicy character, yet isn't overwhelming. Overall, this is one GREAT recipe- thank you, so very, very much! :o)

text:
Excellent sandwich recipe. I did use others suggestions and used sirloin steak. I did marinate the beef and broiled it (too cold to grill) then sliced it thin and added it to the bun with the peppers and onions. The garlic mayo is a must. I have some picky eaters who aren't thrilled with the full raw flavor of garlic so I roasted a head of garlic in the oven for 30 minutes and then mashed it well and added it to about 2 cups of mayo, I was doubling the recipe. Next time I try this I think I might also make up some Sour Cream And Horseradish Sauce, I think that would go very nicely with this. Great easy recipe and yummy.

text:
UPDATE: MADE THESE AGAIN, BUT THIS TIME, I USED ROUND STEAK. I WAS TOO LAZY TO USE MY MEAT SLICER (I STILL THINK THIS IS KEY), BUT WAS VERY CAREFUL TO CUT MY MEAT SUPER THIN. I ALSO DIDN'T COOK IT VERY LONG (I LEFT IT MEDIUM-WELL) AND S&P'D REALLY WELL (NO SEASONING THIS TIME AROUND). MY MEAT WAS VERY TENDER AND OH SO YUMMY! NOT ONLY IS THE THICKNESS OF YOUR MEAT IMPORTANT, NOT OVERCOOKING IT IS EQUALLY IMPORTANT. SUPERB! Nothing compares to the "real" deal, but even so, this wasn't bad at all. The garlic mayo REALLY kicks this up a notch! On the flipside, I think my hubs and I would have liked this MUCH better if our meat was sliced razor thin (albeit I tried my best to slice mine VERY thin). Although I used sandwich steaks instead of round steak (butcher's recommendation), they were still a far too thick. Bottom line, unless you slice your own beef PAPER thin (or with a meat slicer), your sandwich won't be truly "authentic." I'd also like to note that it's IMPERATIVE to remove your meat when you saute your bell peppers / onions. By the time my veggies were crisp tender, my meat was overcooked. :( Other than subbing sandwich steaks and altering the cooking method slightly, my only other change was seasoning my beef with Montreal steak seasoning about a half hour before preparing our sandwiches. Served with french fries and our favorite beer, this was a decent meal. Leftovers will make yummy fajitas. Thanks for sharing your recipe, Tera! :-)

text:
These were SO AMAZING! I attempted to make cheesesteaks once before & the result was just so-so, so my expectations were low to begin with. These blew me away! 

I added some Mrs. Dash to the garlic mayo & used one green and one red pepper for color & flavor. I marinated the meat in some soy sauce, Worcestershire, & A1 for about an hour before cooking. I sauteed the onions and peppers separately with some seasonings & a little sugar to caramelize. The savory meat with the sweet onions & peppers was a to-die-for combination! I used sourdough hoagies and skipped the oregano.

text:
I will agree that this isn't a typical philly cheesesteak.  However, it was very good with the adjustments I made.  I put montreal steak seasoning on the steak strips and sauteed with butter and the minced garlic. I find that for me, using oil cooks my meat too fast and makes it tough.  I added some worcestershire sauce as well and then added the onion, bell pepper, some fresh mushrooms and some italian seasoning.  I baked for about 5 min and then broiled for a few so the cheese got brown and the rolls got crispy on the top.  We didn't use any mayonnaise.  It turned out very well.

text:
Awesome!  I followed another reviewer's advice and bought sirloin steak, seasoned it with steak seasonings (+1 Tbl. olive oil), and marinated it in the refrigerator overnight.  My only mistake was cutting the meat in slices before marinating.  I think I should have left the meat as packaged, marinated it, and then sauteed it.  Although I marinated it with seasonings, I still needed to sprinkle it with salt and pepper after cooking.  Garlic in the mayonnaise is key!  I sprinkled the dried oregano (leaves, not powder!) on the mayonnaise that I spread on the bread, and it toasted up very nicely.  I sauteed the peppers and onions separately in 1 Tbl. olive oil - it took a while to cook and would have dried out the meat if I hadn't.  Thanks for the recipe!

text:
This is a weekly favorite at my house. We use a thin top sirloin instead of the round steak. We usually skip the garlic mayo; it's not really a must for us. We like our food quite a bit spicier, so I add jalapenos to cook with the vegetables. I cook the meat with some soy sauce and a hot sauce mixture. I always cook the vegetables first and then add them to the meat once it is almost done. This way the vegetables absorb some of the flavor and the meat does not get overcooked. You can also change it up and substitute shredded chicken for the steak. Yummy!

This is good. I made some changes. I used flank steak that we grilled to medium rare. Let it rest. I cooked red and yellow bell peppers, onions, sliced mushrooms, 1 tsp of dried rosemary and a few splashes of Worcestershire sauce in olive oil on high heat until caramelized. I cut the flank steak against the grain into slim slices. I took several pieces of steak and made a pile of steak topped with Swiss cheese on a cookie sheet under the broiler until melted. I  spread the garlic mayo onto naan bread, with the steak, grilled veges and some A-1. Delicious!

text:
I had seen this on the recipe buzz quite a few times and finally decided to try it. I had to lighten it up a bit for health reasons, but not for taste. I used lite mayo and cheese, and only half suggested, and a lean cut of beef. I thought it tasted like something that would come from a restaurant. If I ever made again I would make sure the beef is close to paper thin and use a soft bun. It was a bit much to chew with a crustier sub roll and the beef cut a little too thick by the store's butcher. I would also think about dividing it among 8 small buns, instead of 4, as 1/2 sandwich would have been plenty. I think the garlic and oregano really added extra flavor. I can see why there are a lot of high ratings for this sandwich.

text:
THIS IS AWESOME. But I did some things differently... Cut the steaks into thin strips & seasoned with steak spice then let marinate roughly 2 hours (overnight would be best to infuse the flavour more). I then prepared the garlic mayo using the mayo, 3-4 cloves of garlic & a tsp. of wasabi (horseradish) powder to intensify the 'kick'; let it meld in the fridge for a few hours. I caramelized onions and mushrooms until they were golden then used the leftover butter/EVOO to saute green & red bell pepper strips which were seasoned with S&P. Cooked the steaks med-rare (more rare than med). Assembled as such: sour dough bread, garlic mayo, steak, pepper mixture, onion-mushroom mixture & cheese. Cooked as directed. Grated the mozza and mixed it with the oregano. Toasted the tops of the sandwich in a frying pan (they were also spread with the garlic mayo). WOAH, so good. These will definitely make it on my menu as a treat every so often! Served it with a green salad.

text:
I made these sandwiches for dinner the other night and they turned out great! I did make a few changes, however. First, I used sirloin steak and I first rubbed it with Montreal steak seasoning and then slow cooked it for a couple hours on high in some Italian dressing, beer, and beef stock. Then, I cut it into thin strips (which is much easier to do after its cooked!) and threw it in a wok with the onions and peppers (I used one red, and one green) with some olive oil, and heated on medium-high heat until the veggies were tender. This was the first time both me and my husband had had Philly cheese steaks and they were great! And I'm sure more healthier than most restaurants' versions! Will definately make these again!

text:
Excellent. I tried to make Philly cheesesteak sandwiches like those we ate in Philly. First mix up the garlic mayo - it's delicious.  I carmelized onion and set aside.  We do not like green peppers so I skipped those. I used sirloin, sliced thin by the meat dept.  I may try to use ribeye next time, because ribeye meat is so much more tender and has more flavor (it's just harder to slice thin).   I sliced the meat into strips of uniform size.  Cooked meat according to directions.  Sliced and toasted ciabatta rolls in the oven. Spread mayo mixture on rolls and on top of the mayo mixture spread on a generous helping of some warm Cheese Whiz - which they use in Philly.  The ciabatta rolls are nice because they are sturdy and have little nooks for the mayo, juices and Cheese Whiz. Then topped each sandwich with meat. Badabingbadaboom.  We all thought we were in Philly instead of Phoenix.

I brought home a little petite filet mignon when we were out to dinner the other night so I decided to use it to make this sandwich. Left out the mayo, marinated the meat for a couple of hours in 1/2 cup of red wine, a couple splashes of OJ and 1/2 squeezed lemon, then grilled it instead of pan frying. Sprinkled some dill ontop the peppers and onions while cooking. Also used fresh Mexican "Bolillo" rolls and 1/2 pepperjack cheese and 1/2 mozzarella cheese. And whatever you do, melt some cheese in with the beef and pepper mixture before filling the sandwiches! Adding a sliced jalapeno chile marinated in vinegar will kick it up to a nice spicy flavor too! I served an aujou on the side, made with a can of beef broth, some garlic powder and minced onions. Wasn't really necessary, but, some people liked it.

text:
I'm just going to call mine a Great American Steak Sandwich so as not to offend the much too sensitive Philly's.  I have been making this sandwich for quite some time.  Rather than cook my steak in olive oil, I season it with garlic, onion, steak seasoning and a generous amount of soy sauce.  Also, I only use either mozz cheese or provolone.  Once the steak and cheese are on the bread, I throw it in the oven on broil for a few minutes to melt the cheese.  I also put shredded lettuce and tomato slices on top.  This is one of my favorite dinners.

text:
Awesome sandwich with the fresh garlic being the key.  Changes I made was
Add some warmed Philly cream cheese to the mayo mix. 
Let mayo mix sit in frig minimum 30min for flavor melding.
Added mushrooms.
Browned sirloin whole then let rest.
After steak rests, slice steak thinly cross grain
Add steak to back to pan along with juices that were generated while resting and heat steak back up, low heat.
Can mix in a little dried Italian salad mix with steak
Used Harvarti cheese
Broil open faced
For tender meat make sure its cross grain meaning after a slice the meat should pull apart if you stretch it.

text:
Simply delicious.  

I have several vacuum bags of thin-sliced bottom round and decided to try this recipe to use some of that beef up. The flavors were delicious.  I think there are too many peppers and onions for the amount of meat though. Next time I will definitely only use one onion and pepper to keep it on the meatier side.

I used bottom round which has a nice beefy flavor but tends to be a bit chewy.  I negated the chewiness by using a velveting technique on the beef.  After a one-hour marinate in the fridge - it had the perfect texture.

text:
EXCELLENT! I am not a red meat eater but made this for my bf who really loves his steaks. I followed this recipe exactly except I used a boneless ribeye because that's what he always buys. HUGE TIP for everyone. If your steak is frozen, thaw for about a half hour, then slice with a very sharp knife. You'll get paper thin slices! Or freeze a thawed one for 30-60 minutes and do the same. Anyway, he mentioned that a smoked cheese next time might be awesome (yes, I know it's not authentic.....), like a smoked mozz, provalone or cheddar. But he absolutely loved this! Another tip, if you are using a less expensive steak, slice it and marinate in buttermilk all day. Will really soften your meat up!!! Anyway, the garlic mayo was a huge hit. I made it in the morning to let the flavors marry. He LOVED it!!! Thank you!!!!!!!

city:

country:
None
text:
Good food.  I made several modifications based on experience.  I used sweet onions, which together with the bell peppers I caramelized in butter rather than olive oil (bread and butter, as well as onions and butter, pair well) for about 35 minutes on low/medium-low heat.  I lightly toasted the hoagie rolls so they wouldn't get soggy.  I used slightly less onion, about one and a half, and about half the amount of the aioli.   For the steak, I used chuck eye, but rib eye would also do; I wanted something that would be tender rather than chewy.  I salted it thoroughly and cut it thinly against the grain, which worked well.  I served this with seasoned steak fries.  I think a light green salad with a vinaigrette would also be a good side dish, since the sandwich is rather heavy.

The overall idea of the recipe is fine, but it needs some tweaking. I used two 1 pound rib eyes to balance out the veggie to meat ratio. The size of the veggies should be mentioned.  I did 1 regular onion, 2 bell peppers, but i will switch one green for a red next time for some color and a little sweetness. I will add mushrooms next time too. I added a little Worcestershire sauce and some cholula hot sauce for a little kick. I switched out the mozzarella for provolone cause I know that is more traditional, but really both cheeses will work fine, if you already have mozzarella, then no need to buy provolone.

text:
Wasn't a fan of the mayo garlic spread but that's easy to eliminate. I did find that for the portion of meet it was a lot of vegetables. I did 1.5 lbs serloin , seasoned it and let it sit in the fridge for a few hours. 1 onion , 2 peppers and added 3 mushrooms. Had lots of leftover veggies and that was with the extra half pound meat. I'd saw if you did the 1 lb meat you would be fine with 1 small onion and 1 medium bell pepper. Also should add, it's important to pre heat the oven right before you start cooking because if not I found it wasn't hot enough yet to toast the bun by the time the cheese melted.

text:
Wow--excellent sandwich!  I've been exploring different things to do with leftover roast, instead of just using my standard beef stroganoff recipe all the time.  I thought about the idea of a philly cheesesteak, and went on Allrecipes looking for one.  Here is where I ended up, and I couldn't have been happier!  I used 1 onion, 1 pepper, and 1 pound of leftover roast, and ended up with plenty of good, proportionate filling.  Since my meat was already cooked, I let my veggies (especially my onions) get a head start so they could properly caramelize, then added the beef last to heat through.  (I guess I ended up with a cheese-roast sandwich instead of a cheesteak?  Something to ask a true Philadephian!)  The garlic mayo does so much for this recipe--delicious!  Thank you!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I have been making the Philly Cheesesteak sandwich for a couple of years.  I don't bother with purchasing any kind of particular steak.
I buy the the steak meat that is located in the frozen section of my local grocery store.  The brand is called "Philly Steaks" these are very thin and consists of 16 slices per box.  I break apart the meat using my fingers or in the pan while frying with a fork.  This is so easy and the meat fries up in seconds.  While the meat is frying I add chopped onions & green pepper.  I use mozarella or provolone cheese to the roll, microwave the roll (15-20) sec till cheese is partially melted, then add the steak w/the onions and add your other condiments as you wish.  Another alternative is, omit the lettuce, tomato and mayo.  While the steak and onions are cooking, drain off grease and add Pizza Sauce to the steak and onion and mix togeather, then add to your sub roll with the provolone or mozarella cheese to have a Pizza Steak Sub.  This is very good.

What it isn't: a proper Philly cheesesteak. What is is: insanely delicious.  I go to college in Philadelphia, so I have plenty of opportunities to eat "authentic" cheesesteaks.  This cheesesteak sandwich, in my opinion, is better than those.  For one thing, it's not greasy.  I also use boneless sirloin, which is a step up from what you'll get in Philly.  And the garlic mayo.  Oh man, the garlic mayo.  It makes the sandwich go from good to awesome.  Like I said, it's not authentic, but it's ridiculously delicious.

The garlic mayo was good, I added a little horse radish to it to give it a kick.  Also, a cheaper alternative is to use a whole loaf of french bread as opposed to hoagie rolls.   This makes a lot of mayo, if you cut it back by a 1/3 you'll be fine.

text:
My family and I LOVED, LOVED these sandwiches.  The Garlic Mayo was fabulous.  It really made the sandwiches and was SO simple to prepare.  I made these with leftover grilled sirloin steak and it was a fabulous way to use up the steak.  I also added mushrooms to the mix.  Thanks for the great recipe!  I'll definitely be making these again.  BTW, if you don't think the garlic mayo is zippy enough, you probably didn't use enough garlic or put enough mayo on the sandwiches.  You want to slather it on generously.  Also, if you let the mayo sit in the fridge for a couple of hours before you use it, the flavors will be a lot stronger because they've had time to marinade.
